140→\t\t\tcallOpts:     callOpts,\n   141→\t\t\tctx:          ctx,\n   142→\t\t\tstreamerCall: func(ctx context.Context) (grpc.ClientStream, error) {\n   143→\t\t\t\treturn streamer(ctx, desc, cc, token based on the error and callOptions,\n   151→// and returns a boolean value.\n   152→func (c *Client) shouldRefreshToken(err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n   153→\tif c.Token != \"\" {\n   154→\t\t// do not try to refresh the token as it is set by user\n   155→\t\treturn false\n   156→\t}\n   157→\n   158→\tif errors.Is(rpctypes.Error(err), rpctypes.ErrUserEmpty) {\n   159→\t\t// refresh the token when username, password is present but the server returns ErrUserEmpty\n   160→\t\t// which is possible when the client token is cleared somehow\n   161→\t\treturn c.authTokenBundle != nil // equal to c.Username != \"\" && c.Password != \"\"\n   162→\t}\n   163→\n   164→\treturn callOpts.retryAuth &&\n   165→\t\t(errors.Is(rpctypes.Error(err), rpctypes.ErrInvalidAuthToken) || errors.Is(rpctypes.Error(err), rpctypes.ErrAuthOldRevision))\n   166→}\n   167→\n   168→func (c *Client) refreshToken(ctx context.Context) error {\n   169→\tif c.authTokenBundle == nil {\n   170→\t\t// c.authTokenBundle will be initialized only when\n   171→\t\t// c.Username != \"\" && c.Password != \"\".\n   172→\t\t//\n   173→\t\t// When users use the TLS CommonName based authentication, the\n   174→\t\t// authTokenBundle is always nil. But it's possible for the clients\n   175→\t\t// to get `rpctypes.ErrAuthOldRevision` response when the clients\n   176→\t\t// concurrently modify auth data (e.g, addUser, deleteUser etc.).\n   177→\t\t// In this case, there is no need to refresh the token; instead the\n   178→\t\t// clients just need to retry the operations (e.g. Put, Delete etc).\n   179→\t\treturn nil\n   180→\t}\n   181→\n   182→\treturn c.getToken(ctx)\n   183→}\n   184→\n   185→// type serverStreamingRetryingStream is the implementation of grpc.ClientStream that acts as a\n   186→// proxy to the underlying call. If any of the RecvMsg() calls fail, it will try to reestablish\n   187→// a new ClientStream according to the retry policy.\n   188→type serverStreamingRetryingStream struct {\n   189→\tgrpc.ClientStream\n   190→\tclient        *Client\n   191→\tbufferedSends []any // single message that the client can sen\n   192→\treceivedGood  bool  // indicates whether any prior receives were successful\n   193→\twasClosedSend bool  // indicates that CloseSend was closed\n   194→\tctx           context.Context\n   195→\tcallOpts      *options\n   196→\tstreamerCall  func(ctx context.Context) (grpc.ClientStream, error)\n   197→\tmu            sync.RWMutex\n   198→}\n   199→\n   200→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) setStream(clientStream grpc.ClientStream) {\n   201→\ts.mu.Lock()\n   202→\ts.ClientStream = clientStream\n   203→\ts.mu.Unlock()\n   204→}\n   205→\n   206→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) getStream() grpc.ClientStream {\n   207→\ts.mu.RLock()\n   208→\tdefer s.mu.RUnlock()\n   209→\treturn s.ClientStream\n   210→}\n   211→\n   212→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) SendMsg(m any) error {\n   213→\ts.mu.Lock()\n   214→\ts.bufferedSends = append(s.bufferedSends, m)\n   215→\ts.mu.Unlock()\n   216→\treturn s.getStream().SendMsg(m)\n   217→}\n   218→\n   219→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) CloseSend() error {\n   220→\ts.mu.Lock()\n   221→\ts.wasClosedSend = true\n   222→\ts.mu.Unlock()\n   223→\treturn s.getStream().CloseSend()\n   224→}\n   225→\n   226→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) Header() (metadata.MD, error) {\n   227→\treturn s.getStream().Header()\n   228→}\n   229→\n   230→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) Trailer() metadata.MD {\n   231→\treturn s.getStream().Trailer()\n   232→}\n   233→\n   234→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) RecvMsg(m any) error {\n   235→\tattemptRetry, lastErr := s.receiveMsgAndIndicateRetry(m)\n   236→\tif !attemptRetry {\n   237→\t\treturn lastErr // success or hard failure\n   238→\t}\n   239→\n   240→\t// We start off from attempt 1, because zeroth was already made on normal SendMsg().\n   241→\tfor attempt := uint(1); attempt < s.callOpts.max; attempt++ {\n   242→\t\tif err := waitRetryBackoff(s.ctx, attempt, s.callOpts); err != nil {\n   243→\t\t\treturn err\n   244→\t\t}\n   245→\t\tnewStream, err // TODO(mwitkow): Maybe dial and transport errors should be retriable?\n   249→\t\t}\n   250→\t\ts.setStream(newStream)\n   251→\n   252→\t\ts.client.GetLogger().Warn(\"retrying RecvMsg\", zap.Error(lastErr))\n   253→\t\tattemptRetry, lastErr = s.receiveMsgAndIndicateRetry(m)\n   254→\t\tif !attemptRetry {\n   255→\t\t\treturn lastErr\n   256→\t\t}\n   257→\t}\n   258→\treturn lastErr\n   259→}\n   260→\n   261→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) receiveMsgAndIndicateRetry(m any) (bool, error) {\n   262→\ts.mu.RLock()\n   263→\twasGood := s.receivedGood\n   264→\ts.mu.RUnlock()\n   265→\terr := s.getStream().RecvMsg(m)\n   266→\tif err == nil || errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {\n   267→\t\ts.mu.Lock()\n   268→\t\ts.receivedGood = true\n   269→\t\ts.mu.Unlock()\n   270→\t\treturn false, err\n   271→\t} else if wasGood {\n   272→\t\t// previous RecvMsg in the stream succeeded, no retry logic should interfere\n   273→\t\treturn false, err\n   274→\t}\n   275→\tif isContextError(err) {\n   276→\t\tif s.ctx.Err() != nil {\n   277→\t\t\treturn false, err\n   278→\t\t}\n   279→\t\t// its the callCtx deadline or cancellation, in which case try again.\n   280→\t\treturn true, err\n   281→\t}\n   282→\tif s.client.shouldRefreshToken(err, s.callOpts) {\n   283→\t\tgtErr := s.client.refreshToken(s.ctx)\n   284→\t\tif gtErr != nil {\n   285→\t\t\ts.client.GetLogger().Warn(\"retry failed to fetch new auth token\", zap.Error(gtErr))\n   286→\t\t\treturn false, err // return the original error for simplicity\n   287→\t\t}\n   288→\t\treturn true, err\n   289→\t}\n   290→\treturn isSafeRetry(s.client, err, s.callOpts), err\n   291→}\n   292→\n   293→func (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) reestablishStreamAndResendBuffer(callCtx context.Context) (grpc.ClientStream, error) {\n   294→\ts.mu.RLock()\n   295→\tbufferedSends := s.bufferedSends\n   296→\ts.mu.RUnlock()\n   297→\tnewStream, err := s.streamerCall(callCtx)\n   298→\tif err != nil {\n   299→\t\treturn nil, err\n   300→\t}\n   301→\tfor _, msg := range bufferedSends {\n   302→\t\tif err := newStream.SendMsg(msg); err != nil {\n   303→\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   304→\t\t}\n   305→\t}\n   306→\tif err := newStream.CloseSend(); err != nil {\n   307→\t\treturn nil, err\n   308→\t}\n   309→\treturn newStream, nil\n   310→}\n   311→\n   312→func waitRetryBackoff(ctx context.Context, attempt uint, callOpts *options) error {\n   313→\twaitTime := time.Duration(0)\n   314→\tif attempt > 0 {\n   315→\t\twaitTime = callOpts.backoffFunc(attempt)\n   316→\t}\n   317→\tif waitTime > 0 {\n   318→\t\ttimer := time.NewTimer(waitTime)\n   319→\t\tselect {\n   320→\t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n   321→\t\t\ttimer.Stop()\n   322→\t\t\treturn contextErrToGRPCErr(ctx.Err())\n   323→\t\tcase <-timer.C:\n   324→\t\t}\n   325→\t}\n   326→\treturn nil\n   327→}\n   328→\n   329→// isSafeRetry returns \"true\", if request is safe for retry with the given error.\n   330→func isSafeRetry(c *Client, err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n   331→\tif isContextError(err) {\n   332→\t\treturn false\n   333→\t}\n   334→\n   335→\t// Situation when learner refuses RPC it is supposed to not serve is from the server\n   336→\t// perspective not retryable.\n   337→\t// But for backward-compatibility reasons we need  to support situation that\n   338→\t// customer provides mix of learners (not yet voters) and voters with an\n   339→\t// expectation to pick voter in the next attempt.\n   340→\t// TODO: Ideally client should be 'aware' which endpoint represents: leader/voter/learner with high probability.\n   341→\tif errors.Is(err, rpctypes.ErrGRPCNotSupportedForLearner) && len(c.Endpoints()) > 1 {\n   342→\t\treturn true\n   343→\t}\n   344→\n   345→\tswitch callOpts.retryPolicy {\n   346→\tcase repeatable:\n   347→\t\treturn isSafeRetryImmutableRPC(err)\n   348→\tcase nonRepeatable:\n   349→\t\treturn isSafeRetryMutableRPC(err)\n   350→\tdefault:\n   351→\t\tc.GetLogger().Warn(\"unrecognized retry policy\", zap.String(\"retryPolicy\", callOpts.retryPolicy.String()))\n   352→\t\treturn false\n   353→\t}\n   354→}\n   355→\n   356→func isContextError(err error) bool {\n   357→\treturn status.Code(err) == codes.DeadlineExceeded || status.Code(err) == codes.Canceled\n   358→}\n   359→\n   360→func contextErrToGRPCErr(err error) error {\n   361→\tswitch {\n   362→\tcase errors.Is(err, context.DeadlineExceeded):\n   363→\t\treturn status.Error(codes.DeadlineExceeded, err.Error())\n   364→\tcase errors.Is(err, context.Canceled):\n   365→\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Canceled, err.Error())\n   366→\tdefault:\n   367→\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unknown, err.Error())\n   368→\t}\n   369→}\n   370→\n   371→var defaultOptions = &options{\n   372→\tretryPolicy: nonRepeatable,\n   373→\tmax:         0, // disable\n   374→\tbackoffFunc: backoffLinearWithJitter(50*time.Millisecond /*jitter*/, 0.10),\n   375→\tretryAuth:   true,\n   376→}\n   377→\n   378→// backoffFunc denotes a family of functions that control the backoff duration between call retries.\n   379→//\n   380→// They are called with an identifier of the attempt, and should return a time the system client should\n   381→// hold off for. If the time returned is longer than the `context.Context.Deadline` of the request\n   382→// the deadline of the request takes precedence and the wait will be interrupted before proceeding\n   383→// with the next iteration.\n   384→type backoffFunc func(attempt uint) time.Duration\n   385→\n   386→// withRepeatablePolicy sets the repeatable policy of this call.\n   387→func withRepeatablePolicy() retryOption {\n   388→\treturn retryOption{applyFunc: func(o *options) {\n   389→\t\to.retryPolicy = repeatable\n   390→\t}}\n   391→}\n   392→\n   393→// withMax sets the maximum number of retries on this call, or this interceptor.\n   394→func withMax(maxRetries uint) retryOption {\n   395→\treturn retryOption{applyFunc: func(o *options) {\n   396→\t\to.max = maxRetries\n   397→\t}}\n   398→}\n   399→\n   400→// WithBackoff sets the `BackoffFunc` used to control time between retries.\n   401→func withBackoff(bf backoffFunc) retryOption {\n   402→\treturn retryOption{applyFunc: func(o *options) {\n   403→\t\to.backoffFunc = bf\n   404→\t}}\n   405→}\n   406→\n   407→type options struct {\n   408→\tretryPolicy retryPolicy\n   409→\tmax         uint\n   410→\tbackoffFunc backoffFunc\n   411→\tretryAuth   bool\n   412→}\n   413→\n   414→// retryOption is a grpc.CallOption that is local to clientv3's retry interceptor.\n   415→type retryOption struct {\n   416→\tgrpc.EmptyCallOption // make sure we implement private after() and before() fields so we don't panic.\n   417→\tapplyFunc            func(opt *options)\n   418→}\n   419→\n   420→func reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(opt *options, retryOptions []retryOption) *options {\n   421→\tif len(retryOptions) == 0 {\n   422→\t\treturn opt\n   423→\t}\n   424→\toptCopy := &options{}\n   425→\t*optCopy = *opt\n   426→\tfor _, f := range retryOptions {\n   427→\t\tf.applyFunc(optCopy)\n   428→\t}\n   429→\treturn optCopy\n   430→}\n   431→\n   432→func filterCallOptions(callOptions []grpc.CallOption) (grpcOptions []grpc.CallOption, retryOptions []retryOption) {\n   433→\tfor _, opt := range callOptions {\n   434→\t\tif co, ok := opt.(retryOption); ok {\n   435→\t\t\tretryOptions = append(retryOptions, co)\n   436→\t\t} else {\n   437→\t\t\tgrpcOptions = append(grpcOptions, opt)\n   438→\t\t}\n   439→\t}\n   440→\treturn grpcOptions, retryOptions\n   441→}\n   442→\n   443→// BackoffLinearWithJitter waits a set period of time, allowing for jitter (fractional adjustment).\n   444→//\n   445→// For example waitBetween=1s and jitter=0.10 can generate waits between 900ms and 1100ms.\n   446→func backoffLinearWithJitter(waitBetween time.Duration, jitterFraction float64) backoffFunc {\n   447→\treturn func(attempt uint) time.Duration {\n   448→\t\treturn jitterUp(waitBetween, jitterFraction)\n   449→\t}\n   450→}\n   451→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. This behaviour can be\n// changed through options (e.g. WithMax) on creation of the interceptor or on call (through grpc.CallOptions).\nfunc (c *Client) unaryClientInterceptor(optFuncs ...retryOption) grpc.UnaryClientInterceptor {\n\tintOpts := reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(defaultOptions, optFuncs)\n\treturn func(ctx context.Context, method string, req, reply any, cc *grpc.ClientConn, invoker grpc.UnaryInvoker, opts ...grpc.CallOption) error {\n\t\tctx = withVersion(ctx)\n\t\tgrpcOpts, retryOpts := filterCallOptions(opts)\n\t\tvar p peer.Peer\n\t\tgrpcOpts = append(grpcOpts, grpc.Peer(&p))\n\t\tcallOpts := reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(intOpts, retryOpts)\n\t\t// short circuit for simplicity, and avoiding allocations.\n\t\tif callOpts.max == 0 {\n\t\t\treturn invoker(ctx, method, req, reply, cc, grpcOpts...)\n\t\t}\n\t\tvar lastErr error\n\t\tfor attempt := uint(0); attempt < callOpts.max; attempt++ {\n\t\t\tif err := waitRetryBackoff(ctx, attempt, callOpts); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tc.GetLogger().Debug(\n\t\t\t\t\"retrying of unary invoker\",\n\t\t\t\tzap.String(\"target\", cc.Target()),\n\t\t\t\tzap.String(\"method\", method),\n\t\t\t\tzap.Uint(\"attempt\", attempt),\n\t\t\t)\n\t\t\tlastErr = invoker(ctx, method, req, reply, cc, grpcOpts...)\n\t\t\tif lastErr == nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tc.GetLogger().Warn(\n\t\t\t\t\"retrying of unary invoker failed\",\n\t\t\t\tzap.String(\"target\", cc.Target()),\n\t\t\t\tzap.String(\"peer\", p.String()),\n\t\t\t\tzap.String(\"method\", method),\n\t\t\t\tzap.Uint(\"attempt\", attempt),\n\t\t\t\tzap.Error(lastErr),\n\t\t\t)\n\t\t\tif isContextError(lastErr) {\n\t\t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\t// its the context deadline or cancellation.\n\t\t\t\t\treturn lastErr\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t// its the callCtx deadline or cancellation, in which case try again.\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif c.shouldRefreshToken(lastErr, callOpts) {\n\t\t\t\tgtErr := c.refreshToken(ctx)\n\t\t\t\tif gtErr != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\tc.GetLogger().Warn(\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\"retrying of unary invoker failed to fetch new auth token\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\tzap.String(\"target\", cc.Target()),\n\t\t\t\t\t\tzap.Error(gtErr),\n\t\t\t\t\t)\n\t\t\t\t\treturn gtErr // lastErr must be invalid auth token\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif !isSafeRetry(c, lastErr, callOpts) {\n\t\t\t\treturn lastErr\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn lastErr\n\t}\n}\n\n// streamClientInterceptor returns a new retrying stream client interceptor for server side streaming calls.\n//\n// The default configuration of the interceptor is to not retry *at all*. This behaviour can be\n// changed through options (e.g. WithMax) on creation of the interceptor or on call (through grpc.CallOptions).\n//\n// Retry logic is available *only for ServerStreams*, i.e. 1:n streams, as the internal logic needs\n// to buffer the messages sent by the client. If retry is enabled on any other streams (ClientStreams,\n// BidiStreams), the retry interceptor will fail the call.\nfunc (c *Client) streamClientInterceptor(optFuncs ...retryOption) grpc.StreamClientInterceptor {\n\tintOpts := reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(defaultOptions, optFuncs)\n\treturn func(ctx context.Context, desc *grpc.StreamDesc, cc *grpc.ClientConn, method string, streamer grpc.Streamer, opts ...grpc.CallOption) (grpc.ClientStream, error) {\n\t\tctx = withVersion(ctx)\n\t\t// getToken automatically. Otherwise, auth token may be invalid after watch reconnection because the token has expired\n\t\t// (see https://github.com/etcd-io/etcd/issues/11954 for more).\n\t\terr := c.getToken(ctx)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tc.GetLogger().Error(\"clientv3/retry_interceptor: getToken failed\", zap.Error(err))\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tgrpcOpts, retryOpts := filterCallOptions(opts)\n\t\tcallOpts := reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(intOpts, retryOpts)\n\t\t// short circuit for simplicity, and avoiding allocations.\n\t\tif callOpts.max == 0 {\n\t\t\treturn streamer(ctx, desc, cc, method, grpcOpts...)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif desc.ClientStreams {\n\t\t\treturn nil, status.Errorf(codes.Unimplemented, \"clientv3/retry_interceptor: cannot retry on ClientStreams, set Disable()\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tnewStreamer, err := streamer(ctx, desc, cc, method, grpcOpts...)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tc.GetLogger().Error(\"streamer failed to create ClientStream\", zap.Error(err))\n\t\t\treturn nil, err // TODO(mwitkow): Maybe dial and transport errors should be retriable?\n\t\t}\n\t\tretryingStreamer := &serverStreamingRetryingStream{\n\t\t\tclient:       c,\n\t\t\tClientStream: newStreamer,\n\t\t\tcallOpts:     callOpts,\n\t\t\tctx:          ctx,\n\t\t\tstreamerCall: func(ctx context.Context) (grpc.ClientStream, error) {\n\t\t\t\treturn streamer(ctx, desc, cc, method, grpcOpts...)\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn retryingStreamer, nil\n\t}\n}\n\n// shouldRefreshToken checks whether there's a need to refresh the token based on the error and callOptions,\n// and returns a boolean value.\nfunc (c *Client) shouldRefreshToken(err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n\tif c.Token != \"\" {\n\t\t// do not try to refresh the token as it is set by user\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\tif errors.Is(rpctypes.Error(err), rpctypes.ErrUserEmpty) {\n\t\t// refresh the token when username, password is present but the server returns ErrUserEmpty\n\t\t// which is possible when the client token is cleared somehow\n\t\treturn c.authTokenBundle != nil // equal to c.Username != \"\" && c.Password != \"\"\n\t}\n\n\treturn callOpts.retryAuth &&\n\t\t(errors.Is(rpctypes.Error(err), rpctypes.ErrInvalidAuthToken) || errors.Is(rpctypes.Error(err), rpctypes.ErrAuthOldRevision))\n}\n\nfunc (c *Client) refreshToken(ctx context.Context) error {\n\tif c.authTokenBundle == nil {\n\t\t// c.authTokenBundle will be initialized only when\n\t\t// c.Username != \"\" && c.Password != \"\".\n\t\t//\n\t\t// When users use the TLS CommonName based authentication, the\n\t\t// authTokenBundle is always nil. But it's possible for the clients\n\t\t// to get `rpctypes.ErrAuthOldRevision` response when the clients\n\t\t// concurrently modify auth data (e.g, addUser, deleteUser etc.).\n\t\t// In this case, there is no need to refresh the token; instead the\n\t\t// clients just need to retry the operations (e.g. Put, Delete etc).\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\treturn c.getToken(ctx)\n}\n\n// type serverStreamingRetryingStream is the implementation of grpc.ClientStream that acts as a\n// proxy to the underlying call. If any of the RecvMsg() calls fail, it will try to reestablish\n// a new ClientStream according to the retry policy.\ntype serverStreamingRetryingStream struct {\n\tgrpc.ClientStream\n\tclient        *Client\n\tbufferedSends []any // single message that the client can sen\n\treceivedGood  bool  // indicates whether any prior receives were successful\n\twasClosedSend bool  // indicates that CloseSend was closed\n\tctx           context.Context\n\tcallOpts      *options\n\tstreamerCall  func(ctx context.Context) (grpc.ClientStream, error)\n\tmu            sync.RWMutex\n}\n\nfunc (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) setStream(clientStream grpc.ClientStream) {\n\ts.mu.Lock()\n\ts.ClientStream = clientStream\n\ts.mu.Unlock()\n}\n\nfunc (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) getStream() grpc.ClientStream {\n\ts.mu.RLock()\n\tdefer s.mu.RUnlock()\n\treturn s.ClientStream\n}\n\nfunc (s *serverStreamingRetryingStream) SendMsg(m any) error {\n\ts.mu.Lock()\n\ts.bufferedSends = waitRetryBackoff(ctx context.Context, attempt uint, callOpts *options) error {\n\twaitTime := time.Duration(0)\n\tif attempt > 0 {\n\t\twaitTime = callOpts.backoffFunc(attempt)\n\t}\n\tif waitTime > 0 isSafeRetry returns \"true\", if request is safe for retry with the given error.\nfunc isSafeRetry(c *Client, err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n\tif isContextError(err) {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// Situation when learner refuses RPC it is supposed to not serve is from the server\n\t// perspective not retryable.\n\t// But for backward-compatibility reasons we need  to support situation that\n\t// customer provides mix of learners (not yet voters) and voters with an\n\t// expectation to pick voter in the next attempt.\n\t// TODO: Ideally client should be 'aware' which retry policy\", zap.String(\"retryPolicy\", callOpts.retryPolicy.String()))\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc isContextError(err error) bool {\n\treturn status.Code(err) == codes.DeadlineExceeded || status.Code(err) == codes.Canceled\n}\n\nfunc contextErrToGRPCErr(err error) error {\n\tswitch {\n\tcase errors.Is(err, context.DeadlineExceeded):\n\t\treturn status.Error(codes.DeadlineExceeded, defaultOptions = &options{\n\tretryPolicy: nonRepeatable,\n\tmax:         0, // disable\n\tbackoffFunc: backoffLinearWithJitter(50*time.Millisecond /*jitter*/, 0.10),\n\tretryAuth:   true,\n}\n\n// should\n// hold off for. If the time returned is longer than the `context.Context.Deadline` of the request\n// the deadline of the request takes precedence and the wait will be interrupted before proceeding\n// with the next iteration.\ntype backoffFunc func(attempt uint) time.Duration\n\n// withRepeatablePolicy sets the repeatable policy of this call.\nfunc withRepeatablePolicy() retryOption {\n\treturn retryOption{applyFunc: func(o *options) {\n\t\to.retryPolicy = repeatable\n\t}}\n}\n\n// withMax sets the maximum number of retries on this call, or this interceptor.\nfunc withMax(maxRetries uint) retryOption {\n\treturn retryOption{applyFunc: func(o *options) {\n\t\to.max = maxRetries\n\t}}\n}\n\n// WithBackoff sets the `BackoffFunc` used to control time between retries.\nfunc withBackoff(bf backoffFunc) retryOption {\n\treturn retryOption{applyFunc: func(o *options) {\n\t\to.backoffFunc = bf\n\t}}\n}\n\ntype options struct {\n\tretryPolicy retryPolicy\n\tmax         uint\n\tbackoffFunc backoffFunc\n\tretryAuth   bool\n}\n\n// retryOption is a grpc.CallOption that is local to clientv3's retry interceptor.\ntype retryOption struct {\n\tgrpc.EmptyCallOption // make sure we implement private after() and before() fields so we don't panic.\n\tapplyFunc            func(opt *options)\n}\n\nfunc reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(opt *options, retryOptions []retryOption) *options {\n\tif len(retryOptions) == 0 {\n\t\treturn opt\n\t}\n\toptCopy := &options{}\n\t*optCopy = *opt\n\tfor _, f := range retryOptions {\n\t\tf.applyFunc(optCopy)\n\t}\n\treturn optCopy\n}\n\nfunc filterCallOptions(callOptions []grpc.CallOption) (grpcOptions []grpc.CallOption, retryOptions []retryOption) {\n\tfor _, opt := range callOptions {\n\t\tif co, ok := opt.(retryOption); ok {\n\t\t\tretryOptions = append(retryOptions, co)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tgrpcOptions = append(grpcOptions, opt)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn grpcOptions, retryOptions\n}\n\n// BackoffLinearWithJitter waits a set period of time, allowing for jitter (fractional adjustment).\n//\n// For example waitBetween=1s and jitter=0.10 can generate waits between 900ms and 1100ms.\nfunc backoffLinearWithJitter(waitBetween time.Duration, jitterFraction float64) backoffFunc {\n\treturn func(attempt uint) time.Duration {\n\t\treturn jitterUp(waitBetween, jitterFraction)\n\t}\n}\n","numLines":451,"startLine":1,"totalLines":451}}}

between duration\n\t\tn := uint(len(c.Endpoints()))\n\t\tquorum := (n/2 + 1)\n\t\tif attempt%quorum == 0 {\n\t\t\tc.GetLogger().Debug(\"backoff\", zap.Uint(\"attempt\", attempt), zap.Uint(\"quorum\", canceled or timed out, returned \"WatchChan\" is closed,\n\t// and \"WatchResponse\" from this closed channel has zero events and nil \"Err()\".\n\t// The context \"ctx\" MUST be canceled, as soon as watcher is no longer being used,\n\t// to release the associated resources.\n\t//\n\t// If the context is \"context.Background/TODO\", returned \"WatchChan\" will\n\t// not be closed and block until event is triggered, except when server\n\t// returns a non-recoverable error (e.g. ErrCompacted).\n\t// For example, when context passed with \"WithRequireLeader\" and the\n\t// connected server has no leader (e.g. due to network partition),\n\t// error \"etcdserver: no leader\" (ErrNoLeader) will be returned,\n\t// and then \"WatchChan\" is closed with non-nil \"Err()\".\n\t// In order to prevent a watch stream being stuck in a partitioned node,\n\t// make sure to wrap context with \"WithRequireLeader\".\n\t//\n\t// Otherwise, as long as the context has not been canceled or timed out,\n\t// watch will retry on other recoverable errors forever until reconnected.\n\t//\n\t// TODO: explicitly set context error in the last \"WatchResponse\" message and close channel?\n\t// Currently, client contexts are overwritten with \"valCtx\" that never closes.\n\t// TODO(v3.4): configure watch retry policy, limit maximum retry number\n\t// (see https://github.com/etcd-io/etcd/issues/8980)\n\tWatch(ctx context.Context, key string, opts ...OpOption) WatchChan\n\n\t// RequestProgress requests a progress notify response be sent in all watch channels.\n\tRequestProgress(ctx context.Context) error\n\n\t// Close closes the watcher and cancels all watch requests.\n\tClose() error\n}\n\ntype WatchResponse struct {\n\tHeader pb.ResponseHeader\n\tEvents []*Event\n\n\t// CompactRevision is the minimum revision the watcher may receive.\n\tCompactRevision int64\n\n\t// Canceled is used to indicate watch failure.\n\t// If the watch failed and the stream was about to close, before the channel is closed,\n\t// the channel sends a final response that has Canceled set to true with a non-nil Err().\n\tCanceled bool\n\n\t// Created is used to indicate the creation of the watcher.\n\tCreated bool\n\n\tcloseErr error\n\n\t// CancelReason is a reason of canceling watch\n\tCancelReason string\n}\n\n// IsCreate returns true if the event tells that the key is newly created.\nfunc (e *Event) IsCreate() bool {\n\treturn e.Type == EventTypePut && e.Kv.CreateRevision == e.Kv.ModRevision\n}\n\n// IsModify returns true if the event tells that a new value is put on existing key.\nfunc (e *Event) IsModify() bool {\n\treturn e.Type == EventTypePut && e.Kv.CreateRevision != e.Kv.ModRevision\n}\n\n// Err is the error value if this WatchResponse holds an error.\nfunc (wr *WatchResponse) Err() error {\n\tswitch {\n\tcase wr.closeErr != nil:\n\t\treturn v3rpc.Error(wr.closeErr)\n\tcase wr.CompactRevision != 0:\n\t\treturn v3rpc.ErrCompacted\n\tcase wr.Canceled:\n\t\tif len(wr.CancelReason) != 0 {\n\t\t\treturn v3rpc.Error(status.Error(codes.FailedPrecondition, wr.CancelReason))\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn v3rpc.ErrFutureRev\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// IsProgressNotify returns true if the WatchResponse is progress notification.\nfunc (wr *WatchResponse) IsProgressNotify() bool {\n\treturn len(wr.Events) == 0 && !wr.Canceled && !wr.Created && wr.CompactRevision == 0 && wr.Header.Revision != 0\n}\n\n// watcher implements the Watcher interface\ntype watcher struct {\n\tremote   pb.WatchClient\n\tcallOpts []grpc.CallOption\n\n\t// mu protects the grpc streams map\n\tmu sync.Mutex\n","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1044}}}

the core retry logic through `unaryClientInterceptor` and `streamClientInterceptor` functions. These interceptors wrap gRPC calls and implement retry semantics with exponential backoff. The `serverStreamingRetryingStream` type handles stream-specific retry logic by buffering messages and reestablishing connections on failure. Key functions include `isSafeRetry`, `isSafeRetryImmutableRPC`, and `isSafeRetryMutableRPC` which determine whether a request can be safely retried based on the error type and whether it's a read (immutable) or write (mutable) operation.\\n\\n## Endpoint Balancer\\nThe `client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go` implements `EtcdManualResolver` which manages endpoint addresses and configures the gRPC resolver with a round-robin load balancing policy. The health check is performed during client initialization with a configurable timeout and handles cases where the health endpoint may not be implemented.\\n\\n## Request Timeout Enforcement\\nTimeout enforcement is distributed across multiple files:\\n\\n### KV Operations (`client/v3/kv.go`)\\nThe KV service wraps the proto client with `RetryKVClient` which applies repeatable (read) and non-repeatable (write) retry policies. The `NewKV` function initializes the KV service with call options from the client configuration, which include timeout settings and message size limits.\\n\\n### Watch Operations (`client/v3/watch.go`)\\nWatch operations support streaming with context-based timeout control. The Watcher interface documents that context cancellation or timeout results in closed watch channels. The watch implementation uses the provided context for both the stream lifetime and individual message timeouts.\\n\\n### Lease Operations (`client/v3/lease.go`)\\nLease operations through the lessor implement timeout management through:\\n- `firstKeepAliveTimeout`: A timeout for initial keep-alive requests (defaults to 5 seconds or configured DialTimeout)\\n- Context-based timeouts for individual lease operations like `Grant`, `Revoke`, `TimeToLive`, and `Leases`\\n- The KeepAlive streaming operation maintains deadline tracking in the `keepAlive` structure for each lease\\n\\n## Configuration and Timeout Settings\\nThe `client/v3/config.go` defines timeout-related configuration:\\n- `DialTimeout`: Connection establishment timeout\\n- `DialKeepAliveTime`: Keep-alive ping interval\\n- `DialKeepAliveTimeout`: Keep-alive response timeout\\n- `MaxUnaryRetries`: Maximum retry count (defaults to 100)\\n- `BackoffWaitBetween`: Wait time before retry (defaults to 25ms)\\n- `BackoffJitterFraction`: Jitter randomization (defaults to 0.10)\\n\\nThe `client/v3/options.go` file defines default call options including `defaultWaitForReady` (true), message size limits, and retry parameters.\\n\\n## Context and Error Handling\\nThe `client/v3/ctx.go` provides context utilities like `WithRequireLeader` for enforcing leader requirements. The `client/v3/client.go` implements `roundRobinQuorumBackoff` which applies backoff after each round of retry attempts across quorum members, optimizing retry patterns for cluster scenarios.\\n\\n## Endpoint Translation\\nThe `client/v3/internal/endpoint/endpoint.go` handles endpoint URL parsing and credential requirement determination, supporting various schemes (http, https, unix, unixs) and translating them to gRPC-compatible addresses.\\n\\n## Summary\\nThe retry and timeout policy forms a multi-layered system: configuration establishes timeouts and retry limits, the resolver manages endpoint balancing, interceptors apply retry logic with backoff, context controls timeout enforcement at the operation level, and the health check ensures connection validity.
